Because the Mid-Autumn Festival is approaching, both shop owners are settling accounts, and the situation is firmer. New foreign-style rice is arriving sporadically. It is difficult to deliver goods due to the rain, causing prices to continue to rise by 20 cents. Thick and thin broken japonica rice is also up slightly. The rest are unchanged.

Xinzha - About ten ships arrived yesterday. There was no unloding in the morning due to heavy rain. The weather cleared up in the afternoon, but trading was limited. The supply of east and west new japonica rice is not high, rising by 10 cents. New foreign-style pointed rice arrived and sold smoothly. Wholesale prices continued to rise. Early thin rice on the upper wharves and in storage was about 1,000 dan, with prices rising by 5 cents. The situation for northern japonica rice remains unchanged. The shape is stable. There is a slight surplus of foreign rice, with no spot transactions. Futures are quite active, with prices increasing by almost 10 cents.

Foreign Rice Futures Rise by 10 Cents 121

Yesterday, there were few spot transactions of foreign rice. However, warehouse owners and local merchants were inquiring about futures, making the market very active. Furthermore, due to reports of rising prices in the production areas, investor confidence was extremely high. Both new transactions and repurchased goods jumped by about 10 cents. If warehouse owners continue to buy, the market should improve. The entire market offered 200 bags of Mindang spot rice at a price of $12.90. 300 tons of September delivery Xiaojiao futures were repurchased at a price of 5 taels, 6 dimes, and 3 cents to 5 taels, 6 dimes, and 9 cents. Also, 300 tons of October delivery were traded at a price of 5 taels, 7 dimes to 5 taels, 7 dimes, and 3 cents. 700 tons of November delivery Xiaojiao futures were newly traded at a price of 5 taels, 7 dimes, sold by Yuanxing Foreign Firm and bought by local merchants.

Flour Futures Fall by 2.5 Cents 122

Yesterday, the flour market presented a wavering appearance again. The price of foreign wheat in Chicago was up 0.2 to 0.3 dollars, while in Canada it was down a little, showing mixed signals. However, since the sharp changes in the gold market, exchange rates have been rising daily, making foreign wheat prices increasingly cheaper. At a time when the market is already suffering from oversupply, encountering this adverse situation, investor confidence is inevitably shaken. As Russian wheat has already been continuously set for shipment, yesterday it was reported that two ships of Australian white wheat had also been traded at a total price of only 3 taels and 8 dimes. If the market intends to persist in the face of such violent phenomena, it will be difficult to sustain. Therefore, although manufacturers have not engaged in large-scale selling, the sense of uncertainty is gradually increasing. In the near term, due to sluggish sales, there has been a return of long positions in the long term. The market has therefore been declining continuously, with the current month falling to as low as 2 taels, 0 dimes, 4 cents, and 2.5 li, which broadly reflects the market's gloom. As a result, the current month fell by 2 cents and 7 li, October fell by 2 cents and 2.5 li, November fell by 2.5 cents, December and January fell by 2 cents and 2.5 li, and February fell by 2 cents.

Wheat Futures Market Plunges in the Afternoon 123

Another Two Ships of Australian White Wheat Reportedly Set for Shipment

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was relatively calm in the morning after opening, with little change from the previous day's closing price. However, investor confidence suddenly changed when the market opened in the afternoon. Because the flour market had already seen a decline, and the continuous shipment of foreign wheat had become active again, the violent actions of Japan, although universally condemned, have had little impact on foreign orders. With the price of gold short, there are many people looking to sell foreign wheat. For example, another two ships of Australian white wheat were reportedly set for shipment at a price of only 3 taels and several dimes. With such low comparative prices, how could investor confidence not be shaken? Therefore, all months saw declines, with the current month falling to as low as 3 taels and 6 dimes and 8 cents, a record low in the severe decline. Looking ahead, before the door to foreign wheat is closed, long positions must remain cautious. As a result, the current month fell by 6 cents compared to the previous day, October fell by 3 cents, November fell by 4 cents, December fell by 3 cents, January fell by 4 cents, and February fell by 3 cents.

The Sugar Market is Quiet and Steady 124

400 Tons of Raw Sugar Sold Off

Yesterday, sugar market reports from the producing regions indicated that the price of Cuban spot sugar remained unchanged. New York sugar futures for all months rose by 1 to 3 points compared to the previous telegram. Java spot and futures sugar also remained unchanged. Trading in the association market remained sparse. The price of new Dutch No. 24 raw sugar was still 11 taels, 3 dimes, and 7.5 cents. Dutch No. 20 medium sugar was 10 taels, 0 dimes, 9 cents, and 2.5 cents to 9 cents. There were no inquiries about old goods. Dutch No. 9 red sugar was 9 taels and 4 cents. The trends were all steady. Taikoo Refineries' B Mark sugar was 11 taels and 9.5 cents, with sales remaining strong. DY Mark sugar was 11 taels and 8 cents, with a severe shortage of goods. HM Mark sugar was 11 taels, 4 dimes, and 7.5 cents, with the latter trading at 11 taels and 4 dimes and 5 cents. The market was generally very firm. Dachang Foreign Firm sold off 400 tons of old raw sugar to be shipped in October, priced at 5.5 Dutch guilders, new regulations plus tax. The market atmosphere was still lively.

Textiles 125

Cotton Cloth and Western Textiles Rise Together 126

Industry Associations Establish Anti-Japanese Organizations... Stop Trading in Eastern Goods

The textile market is unusually chaotic and on the verge of collapse. Textiles from Japan have occupied nine-tenths of the market in recent years. Although the advanced British and American goods also have difficulty competing with them, the Japanese force is exceptionally powerful. Since the Wanbaoshan Incident, although anti-Japanese associations have been established and inspections have been carried out, a considerable number of goods are still being secretly shipped through the post office. Now that the Japanese are becoming even more rampant, occupying our Eastern Provinces, anyone with a conscience is filled with grief and indignation. Therefore, anti-Japanese associations have been established within the industry, with mutual supervision. Therefore, since the previous day, trading has been impossible. Sales of cotton cloth have been relatively smooth, and prices have risen across the board. Nine-pound coarse cloth, Cat Eagle and Five Blessings, are both priced at 5 taels and 5 cents. Eleven-pound Three Rabbit and Three Deer are priced at 5 taels and 6 dimes and 5 cents. Sixteen-pound goods are selling briskly, and spot goods are quite scarce. Hua Chang's fine cloth and fine twill fabrics are produced in smaller quantities, resulting in a more speculative attitude. Western goods are now very expensive due to the large shortage of inventory. The high prices are unprecedented. Fengyu's 24 Railway cotton is priced at 15 taels and 7.5 cents, and 26 Railway is priced at 16 taels and 5 cents. The 1.6-foot Datian'e original velvet is 1 tael and 5.5 cents. Haoshi Flower Butterfly is 1 tael and 6.5 cents. Yiji original Ning silk is 4 dimes and 5 cents. However, Yuanfang's price calls were slightly lower yesterday due to the unstable situation.

Dried Goods and Lotus Seed Market Prices Loosen 127

Lotus seeds previously had a high price of 32 taels due to tight supply. Now, although market inventory is still insufficient, sales in various regions have gradually decreased, so sales have also loosened. Yesterday, the market price was 30 taels, down 2 taels from the previous day. However, new goods will still take time to arrive, and the market may not improve much.

Silk and Tea European and American Silk Sales Come to a Halt 129

Since Britain announced the suspension of the gold standard, drastic changes have occurred in foreign exchange. Overseas consolidated markets have been suspended for three days, silk telegrams have not been transmitted, and European and American warehouse owners are thinking of hoarding and raising prices. Local Chinese merchants have difficulty selling at original prices. Yesterday, there were no transactions in silk futures or spot silk, and the future of the silk market is increasingly pessimistic.

Gongxi Green Tea Sales to Russia Are Still Smooth 130

For the sake of avenging the compatriots who have already died, and for the sake of the future survival of the nation, representatives from various universities in Shanghai initiated a meeting, which led to the preparation of the All-Circles Anti-Japanese Congress. Like birds with overturned nests, wagtails face urgent difficulties. It is deeply hoped that people from all walks of life in the Northeast who are in Shanghai will actively participate to carry out patriotic movements and save the nation. Yesterday's Expressions from Various Sectors 141

Telegrams from the Four District Party Headquarters Urging Swift Reinforcement of National Defense

The Fourth District Party Headquarters convened an emergency executive committee meeting yesterday. Many opinions were expressed regarding Japan's dispatch of troops to Manchuria. The following is a transcription of their telegram:

To the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Commanders-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force (excerpt omitted):

The reason why Japan is so disrespectful and contemptuous of our country today is that our country is embroiled in a fierce civil war, afflicted by natural disasters, our soldiers are weary, the people are struggling to survive, and, in particular, our military preparations are insufficient to defend against foreign aggression, and our national defense lacks consolidation. Therefore, they do as they please, as if they were in an uninhabited territory. This is partly due to Japan taking advantage of our weakness, but it is also due to our country's neglect of national defense. Today, the invasion of our Northeast by the military is only the first step in their plan. Their ambitions are great and will not stop there. Their northern aggression will inevitably lead to the swallowing of Manchuria and Mongolia, and, in due course, the invasion of China proper. If this were to happen, their southern aggression policy would easily advance simultaneously. At that time, neglecting our front and rear, with a fragile national defense, our country would not be secure. Alas, now that the matter has come to this point, with great disaster looming, all citizens are filled with righteous indignation and vow to save the country. Strengthening national defense is the most urgent task. Concentrating our strength and preparing quickly is even more necessary. We have heard that after occupying Anshan and Huangdao, the Japanese army will move south along the Beining Railway, eyeing our Yuguan. This is something that those who value national defense should pay attention to. Shanhaiguan is currently a strategically important area, the gateway to North China. We should concentrate our strength there immediately to create a defensive fallback position. This is another aspect of national defense that should be noted. The coastal areas, such as Xiamen and Shantou in Fujian, and the Yangtze River region, along with their key ports, should concentrate the military forces of their respective provinces to prepare for any eventuality. This is yet another area that needs solid defense. Nanjing is our country's capital, backed by mountains and facing the sea. The defense of the Yangtze River must not be overlooked, and the Jinpu Railway, which leads directly to the Central Plains, is a critical area. Heavy troops should be stationed there to prepare for resistance. This is another aspect of national defense that should be noted. The plan for now is to first consolidate national defense to prevent the Japanese army from making further advances in their plans. Then, we should gather the strength of the entire country to resist the Japanese army and use military force to compel them to withdraw. Although it is like digging a well when one is already thirsty, it is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep has been lost. If the entire country is of one mind and works together, the Japanese, however cunning, will inevitably bring about their own demise by their many unjust acts. This association, on behalf of the comrades in this district, vows to be a bulwark for the government. Regarding the consolidation of national defense and the concentration of military strength, we humbly offer our suggestions. We earnestly request your careful consideration. This urgent telegram cannot express the extent of our anxiety.

Respectfully, the Fourth District Party Headquarters of Shanghai Special Municipality.

Suggestions from Party Member Shao Xubai. Party member Shao Xubai made three suggestions to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association yesterday. The following are excerpts of the reasons: (excerpt omitted) (1) Our economic severance with Japan has been done repeatedly, but all have quickly fizzled out, only leaving Japanese people scoffing at us. It is truly painful to mention. Therefore, in this anti-Japanese campaign, in addition to being strict with the boycott movement, we should also actively promote domestic goods. Your association should unite with various organizations to form an association for promoting domestic goods, following the methods of the previous anti-Japanese association. Extract funds for saving the nation from Japanese goods to cover expenses or raise funds through other methods, depositing them in a designated bank. At the same time, appoint special personnel to investigate the types and quantities of Japanese goods sold in China. Most importantly, investigate our country's inventions that have not yet been made but are exclusive to Japan, or those that have already been invented but are inferior to Japanese goods (such as mimeograph machines). After the investigation is completed, solicit those with the knowledge or experience to manufacture these goods, enabling them to conduct dedicated research separately. After success, if the quality of the product can exceed that of Japanese goods and the price is equal to or lower than Japanese goods, then request the government to grant the most honorary certificate and a certain number of years of exclusive distribution rights. Our country has vast land and abundant resources. Almost all kinds of raw materials are available, and we are not short of specialized talents. It is only because of economic hardship that those who aspire to research cannot do so, resulting in the neglect of skills, which is truly lamentable. If we can actively carry out this method, the future of domestic goods will truly depend on it.

(2) There are many Japanese merchants and factories in Shanghai, and quite a few Japanese people need to employ Chinese people. Your association should urge them to voluntarily terminate their employment relationships and implement a policy of non-cooperation to halt the commercial and industrial activities of the Japanese in Shanghai. At the same time, request party and government organs to actively find ways to provide alternative employment and inform domestic goods factories to accommodate as many as possible. Other jobs, such as nannies and servants, should also be urged to quit. In this way, their commercial and industrial activities will be hit, and Japanese residents in Shanghai will be panicked.

(3) During each boycott, unscrupulous merchants often take the opportunity to raise the prices of domestic goods to seek profit, which is outrageous and despicable. Therefore, your association should request the authorities to strictly prohibit merchants from hoarding and raising prices. If any of the above-mentioned situations are discovered, they should be regarded as sabotaging the anti-Japanese work. The above three points are of great importance. It is hoped that your association will discuss them in detail, plan their implementation, and promote their realization. I cannot help but offer my sincere wishes.

Telegram from Chen Jiayou in Malaysia. The National Society reports: Chen Jiayou respectfully informs all compatriots in a telegram: (title omitted).

With respect, Japanese imperialists fabricated facts and suddenly used lightning-fast means to destroy and occupy our cities and slaughter our soldiers and civilians. They are still continuing to send land, sea, and air forces to attack in multiple directions without end. Their cruelty has reached the point of turning residences into ruins and flesh and blood into a tragic mess. The shocking news has spread, causing unbearable grief. I believe that their cunning intention to occupy Manchuria and Mongolia and then invade the entire country has been around for a long time. However, it was constrained by the balance of international power and has not been achieved until recently. With Russia and Germany having reached the end of their strength and the United Kingdom and the United States being out of reach, and coupled with our country's successive years of internal wars and common floods, reaching the point of extreme danger, they believe that the time is ripe. Therefore, they disregarded the Kellogg-Briand Pact and righteousness and humanity, and suddenly unleashed their poisonous and ruthless ambition to achieve their long-cherished wish of annexation. At this critical moment of survival or extinction, if our people are willing to be a continuation of India and Korea, so be it. Otherwise, the only option is for the entire nation to rise up as one, uphold the spirit of national self-determination, follow the Prime Minister's advocacy of abolishing unequal treaties, and vow to fight to the last ditch to save a fraction of hope from danger. If we continue to adhere to the policy of non-resistance or hope for international intervention, we are simply waiting for death. As the saying goes, "There is no greater sorrow than a dead heart." Even a trapped beast will fight back without any spare time to look back. The three households that destroyed Qin were truly based on the same hatred of the enemy. Moreover, our country has vast land and abundant resources, a large population, and many soldiers. If we can unite as one and vow to resist insults, how can we not hold up spears to strike at the strong armor and sharp weapons of Qin and Chu? In short, we must bend the chimney before a fire starts and move the firewood away. With the nest overturned, how can there be any unbroken eggs? Today, the only option is to prefer shattering like jade rather than surviving like tile. Only then can we have the possibility of surviving after being placed in a deadly situation. In the aftermath of Jiayou's righteous indignation, I believe that there are three things that should be urgently implemented by the entire nation in this great crisis. I will briefly describe them below:

A. General Mobilization of the National Army: (1) Immediately cease internal wars and organize a national defense conference. (2) All existing troops should be formed into national defense forces, deployed at key points along the river to prevent the enemy from invading, and advance to recover the destroyed and occupied areas (but still use a portion to eliminate the Communist bandits). (3) Expand and unify national ordnance factories. (4) The people should organize volunteer corps as a backing for the national defense forces. (5) The people should organize self-defense forces to maintain rear area security.

B. General Economic Mobilization of the Country: (1) Permanent economic severance with Japan. (2) Issue national defense bonds. (3) Organize national defense donations. (4) Establish national defense logistics stations.

C. General Political Mobilization of the Country: (1) Vow to stop all domestic entertainment and mourn for the national disaster. (2) Conduct thorough and expanded propaganda of righteousness and humanity internationally. (3) Immediately declare the abolition of all unequal treaties with Japan. (4) First form local conferences to elect representatives, then form a national conference. (5) Strictly supervise the government and be tough on foreign affairs. (6) Develop the spirit of national self-determination and thoroughly maintain national independence and sovereignty.

The above three points are truly the only path to survival and national salvation. There must be no hesitation or delay, and even more so, no private interests or prejudices mixed in. If the people of the whole country, without north or south, without factions or affiliations, without division of classes, without division of officials and civilians, can wash away the inertia of abandoning their national duties and act in unison, then perhaps there is hope. These urgent words are followed by tears. I earnestly hope that the elders, brothers, sisters, and siblings of the whole country will be alert and heed them. Jiayou bows, Malaysia.

Some say that women in our country especially like to use Japanese goods because they are cheap and good-looking. Does this unfairly accuse women? The Dutch Ship, Encountering Wind, Sets Sail This Morning

Zhang Ji, Cai Yuanpei, Central Supervisory Committee Members, Chen Mingshu, former Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, Xu Xijun, Chen’s Secretary, and a party of four, came to Shanghai from Beijing the night before last. Hurricane Warning in Shanghai 143

Sea Vessels Suspend Operations

Hurricane Occurs. Yesterday, the Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather report, stating that a hurricane had occurred in the Wenzhou waters. The wind is currently blowing in a northeasterly direction and progressing extremely rapidly. A hurricane had already reached the mouth of the Yangtze River outside Wusong in the afternoon. After this report was released, a large black ball was hung on the weather report stand at the intersection of Huangpu Garden and Edward Road to warn of the impending hurricane in Shanghai, so that the shipping industry could prepare in advance.

Customs Fired Cannons. After receiving the Observatory’s report, the Jianghai Customs immediately fired a signal cannon on the Pudong side at 4:45 PM. This was to warn all shipping companies in Shanghai and ships sailing in the Huangpu River so that they could take precautions in advance to avoid the dangers of the hurricane. After this signal cannon was fired, small sampans, rowing boats, cargo barges, and civilian boats in the Huangpu River suspended operations early. Around 5:00 PM, they all sailed to the old port and the wharves to take shelter from the wind.

Shanghai-Ningbo Vessels Stopped. Yesterday, the Shanghai-Ningbo vessels, the Zhaoshang’s Xin Jiangtian and the Sanbei’s Ningxing, had already loaded passengers and cargo and were preparing to depart at 4:00 PM. Upon receiving the Customs’ hurricane warning, they decided not to depart to avoid danger. The passengers who had already boarded were notified by the crew to go ashore and return home. The departures were rescheduled for Saturday. Those who did not wish to travel could have their tickets refunded. The Jinliyuan Wharf was quite lively for a time as passengers refunded their tickets and returned home. The Taikoo, Ningshao, Xin Beijing, and Xin Ningshao vessels in Ningbo also telegraphed to stay in Ningbo and not depart. Other vessels, such as the Shanghai-Taiwan and Chonghai vessels, did not depart and remained in Shanghai to take shelter from the wind.

Sea Vessels Delayed. Yesterday, the outbound sea vessels included the Taikoo’s Liangzhou and Linan, and the Jardine Matheson’s Fusheng. Except for the Fusheng, which had already departed at 1:00 PM in the afternoon and was later notified by Jardine Matheson via wireless to take shelter from the wind en route, the Linan, Liangzhou, and other vessels did not set sail and remained in Shanghai to take shelter from the wind. The Ninghai, Nanning, and Dalian Maru vessels, which were scheduled to depart for Shantou, Guangdong, and Yingkou (??), Dalian (???) and other ports this morning, had already decided to postpone their departures. Those that still had to travel after the hurricane occurred still had to sail. However, since the wind had already reached the mouth of the Yangtze River this time, the Yangtze River vessels that were scheduled to depart this morning also unanimously postponed their departures to avoid accidents.

Dutch Vessel Moves Slowly. The Java China Japan Lijn’s SS Tjisadane was originally scheduled to depart yesterday. Our Central Committee members Zhang Ji, Cai Yuanpei, and others were traveling on this vessel to Hong Kong and then Guangdong to discuss the overall policy of peace and foreign relations. Unexpectedly, news suddenly arrived that a hurricane was about to strike the local area. The vessel temporarily postponed its departure and rescheduled it for today.

Japanese Tea Amidst the Anti-Japanese Voice. 147

Chinese Tea Sales to Russia Severely Hit.

A Certain Foreign Firm Orders Large Quantities of Japanese Tea.

In recent years, the foreign sales of Chinese tea have been declining day by day. The important reasons for this are that the Chinese are sticking to old methods and do not know how to improve, but the occupation of the European and American markets by Indian and Ceylonese black tea and the encroachment of Japanese green tea on Russia are also reasons. According to an investigation by people in the tea industry, Japanese tea could not be sold to Russia before. However, since 1925 (i.e., the 14th year of the Republic of China), the record of the first export of Japanese tea to Russia was opened, but the amount was only more than 300,000 pounds. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, it jumped to more than one million pounds. In the 18th year, it exceeded three million pounds. Last year, that is, the 19th year of the Republic of China, the total amount of green tea shipped from Shanghai to Russia was 4,777,700 pounds, while Japanese green tea reached 6,154,785 pounds, exceeding Chinese tea. Chinese tea sales to Russia have been severely hit. However, recently, according to the Japanese-language newspaper Shanghai Daily News on the 20th, the Xiexie Foreign Firm in this port has ordered 12,000 boxes of green tea from Japan, about 5,000 dan, and the negotiations have been settled. It is said that the goods must be traded and that the tea leaves are mixed with Chinese green tea by the firm and shipped to the United Kingdom, etc. Japan's aggression against China can be described as meticulous, and it is unknown how the tea industry will deal with the aftermath.

More than 20 cases of discussion on various issues such as engineering, business, and accounting by the members have been submitted to the General Assembly for resolution. Domestic electrical machinery factories, electrical machinery trading foreign firms, and electrical materials dealers in this port are all planning to take this opportunity to bring small samples and gifts to the meeting to participate and make every effort to promote in order to promote business.

Since its opening in June, the National Goods Emporium of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Exhibition Hall has experienced thriving business. Expansions include stationery and toys, tobacco and alcohol, knitwear, leather goods, cotton textiles, and general merchandise. The grand opening is rumored to be on October 1st.

Sheet Four 150

Local News Two

Yesterday's News on Disaster Relief from Various Provinces 151

Two Breaches in the Riverbank of Wuwei County

Wuwei County in Anhui Province is bordered by rivers on three sides, encompassing over a million mu of polder land and over half a million mu of alluvial land, all protected by a single dike line stretching 260 li. On August 14th of this year, the riverbank breached at Huangsitang Port and Temple Port, resulting in a loss of over 40 million yuan for the entire county and affecting over 400,000 disaster victims. Representatives, including Lu Zhi'an, have been dispatched to Shanghai to appeal to the National Government and various charitable organizations. Recently, the representatives received a telegram from the county reporting that two more breaches had occurred at Baiyuchi and Huangnizui in the higher reaches of the riverbank. The inner river water suddenly rose over four chi, causing those disaster victims who had already sought refuge in higher ground to be swept away by the water, resulting in countless deaths. Moreover, the Wuwei riverbank is crucial to the safety of Helu, Shuchao, and Han, six counties. It is said that these six counties have also experienced a water level rise of over three chi in recent days.

Emergency Relief Association Refuses Japanese Relief Funds

Over 100,000 Yuan in Relief Funds Remitted Yesterday

During the ninth meeting of the Standing Committee of the Shanghai Emergency Relief Association for Flood Victims in Various Provinces, someone proposed that disaster victims in various regions have unanimously expressed their refusal to accept relief funds and supplies from Japan. The question was raised whether the association should reconsider its policy. After deliberation, it was decided that all relief funds and supplies from Japan would be rejected and no longer accepted. The National Government Disaster Relief Committee was also requested to handle the matter consistently. The association reportedly requested Mr. Zhu Ziqiao to convey this decision to the National Government Disaster Relief Committee yesterday.

The Emergency Relief Association for Flood Victims in Various Provinces remitted the following relief funds yesterday: (1) 20,000 yuan to Hubei, delivered to Mr. Li Zuoshen in Hankou; (2) 20,000 yuan to Hunan, delivered by Mr. Li Zuoshen to Zhao Youqin; (3) 7,000 yuan to Southern Anhui, delivered to Zhang Gongheng and Qu Zhancheng in Wuhu; (4) 7,000 yuan to Central Anhui, delivered to Xu Pingxuan in Anqing, with an additional remittance of 1,000 yuan; (5) 6,000 yuan to Northern Anhui, delivered to Liu Zhensheng in Bengbu; (6) 20,000 yuan to Jiangsu, delivered to the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association; (7) 20,000 yuan to Henan, delivered to Wang Pinggeng in Kaifeng; (8) 7,500 yuan to Guangdong, to be delivered to the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce after receiving funds from the Chaozhou Association, totaling 100,850 yuan.

Allocation of Relief Funds in Hubei Province Determined

The National Government Disaster Relief Committee received a telegram from Li Jin, the Director of Relief Operations in Hankou, reporting on the allocation of the 110,000 yuan in relief funds previously remitted from Shanghai: (1) 25,000 yuan to each of the counties severely affected by the disaster: Hanchuan, Mianyang, Huanggang, Huangpi, Xiaogan, Tianmen, Huangmei, and Echeng; (2) 16,000 yuan to each of the moderately affected counties: Yingcheng, Guangji, Jiayu, Jiangling, Yangxin, and Xianning; (3) 12,000 yuan to each of the less severely affected counties: Yunmeng, Puqi, Macheng, Anlu, and Xiangyang.

News from the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association

Establishment of the Northern Jiangsu Relief Commissioner's Office

The National Government Disaster Relief Committee has appointed Mr. Cheng Jingsheng as the Northern Jiangsu Relief Commissioner. The commissioner's office has now been established. The association recently received an official letter from the office, which reads as follows: "Dear Sirs, I, Jingsheng, have been appointed by the National Government Disaster Relief Committee as the Northern Jiangsu Relief Commissioner. I immediately traveled to Yangzhou and established an office at No. 42 Zuo Wei Street on September 21st, where I have begun using my official seal and appointing directors of investigation and relief for various counties to handle emergency relief and temporary assistance matters. I am notifying you separately. Sincerely, to the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association."

Overview of the Disaster Situation in Ganyu County. The association received the following report from Ganyu: (The upper part is omitted) "In early August, continuous torrential rains caused widespread flooding. Subsequently, on the night of September 1st, a violent storm raged for eight hours. The already harvested autumn crops were mostly washed away. The beans, which were budding and forming pods, were destroyed. The autumn harvest is completely hopeless. We earnestly hope that all great philanthropists will provide relief." (The lower part is omitted)

Summary of the Jisheng Society's Relief Efforts in Southern Anhui

The Chinese Jisheng Society received a report from Zhai Fengxiang, the Director of Relief Operations in Southern Anhui, stating that the disaster situation in Xuancheng, Wuhu, Dangtu, Nanling, and Fanchang counties in Southern Anhui is extremely severe. The Emergency Relief Association and the Jisheng Society are jointly conducting relief efforts. However, the funds are insufficient to address the scale of the disaster in the five counties. We earnestly request that you raise and allocate more funds to alleviate the suffering. It has been found that, apart from a small number of disaster victims who can find ways to make a living and have already taken refuge elsewhere, those who are sheltering from the wind and rain in makeshift sheds on higher ground and embankments are all destitute. They can only be categorized based on the size of their families: families with three or fewer members are classified as third-class, families with four to five members are classified as second-class, and families with six or more members are classified as first-class. Moreover, the commercial port of Wuhu and the mountainous northern part of Xuancheng have received disaster victims who have migrated from counties such as Hehan. It is impossible to exclude them, so they are being treated equally and investigated for relief. The disaster area in Southern Anhui encompasses ten counties. The relief funds for the five severely affected counties of Xuannan, Dangwu, and Fan are far from sufficient. The situation in other counties, which are beyond our reach, can be imagined. Although the relief funds allocated by the two associations are considerable, they are like a drop in the bucket compared to the vast need. We sincerely hope that you will raise more funds and provide a continuous stream of assistance, so that those who have already received relief can be saved thoroughly, and those who have not yet received relief can still have hope.

Report from Disaster Victims in Yancheng

To the Shen Bao: Calamity has befallen our Yancheng. In the sixteenth year, over 300,000 soldiers passed through, requiring over 500,000 yuan in supplies. In the seventeenth and eighteenth years, we suffered consecutive droughts. Bandits occupied the city, and the losses were countless. Last year, bandits were rampant in the countryside, looting, kidnapping, burning, and killing, turning homes into ruins. The losses were also countless. This year, the rice crop initially showed signs of a good harvest in early summer. However, since entering the fu period, the upper river has opened three dams in succession, releasing floodwaters that submerged the entire region. It was already felt that it would be difficult to protect the crops. Fortunately, the weather was mostly clear, allowing for an early harvest. But misfortune did not come singly. The You Shao Transport Embankment collapsed at the same time, causing rapid and turbulent waves in an instant. All dams collapsed, with no exceptions. The water depth in the city reached over one zhang in deep areas and seven to eight chi in shallow areas. Countless people climbed onto rooftops and treetops, waiting to die. Cries for help could be heard for a hundred li. Fortunately, the water gates and the south gate of the city were blocked in advance, preventing flooding. However, due to leakage from the water gates, areas such as the Northwest Dizang Temple, Yayi Bathhouse, and the public sports field became flooded. The thatched and earthen houses of the poor were completely washed away. If the city was like this, the situation in the countryside can be imagined. Currently, there are over twenty refugee shelters in the city, but only over 5,000 people have been rescued. There are still hundreds of thousands of people who have not been rescued. Can we expect a single city to be able to relieve the disaster of an entire county? Xinghua's terrain is extremely low. Considering this year, the flood disaster is more severe in Yancheng. However, judging from the disasters of the past few years, the situation is unprecedented in Xinghua. Now, after reading the disaster reports in various Shanghai newspapers, the disaster situation in Xia, Xinghua is listed as severe, grouped together with Gao and Bao counties, which is no different from our Dongtai county (Dong has Runlong Port, and Yan has Xinyang Port, the amount of water discharged is the same; Dong has the Dafeng Yuhua Company's sluice gate, and Yan has the Taihe Dayou sluice gate, the harm of blocking and releasing water is also the same, and Dong's terrain is even higher than that of Yan), while the severe disaster situation in Yancheng has not been described in detail. Old Master Dong Zhu Zi of Aviation surveyed the disaster, and Mr. Leng Yuqiu and others stopped at Yu Hua. The disaster situation in Yancheng is mostly based on hearsay from neighboring counties, not a factual record. Those who spread the rumors are not hostile to our Yan, but their intention is nothing more than to reduce one point of disaster in their county and increase one point of relief in their county. At a time when everyone is struggling to save their own lives, such fabricated facts are also a characteristic of disaster areas. It depends on how the listeners perceive them. The so-called great men and gentlemen of Yancheng usually sit on salaries, have many henchmen, are skilled in soliciting lawsuits, and collude with the government for support. They have never cared about the suffering of the people. Even in the face of a major disaster, they show no awareness, enjoy lavish feasts, and laugh as usual. They have not even considered matters such as relief propaganda, resulting in the strange disaster not being widely known and the great relief not being universally applied (Mrs. Hatong donated 50,000 yuan for relief, including Xing and Dong, but not Yancheng, which is clear proof). Is this because the relief providers are abandoning our Yancheng people? It is because our Yancheng people are abandoning themselves. We deeply appreciate the efforts of your newspaper in publicizing this flood disaster. Therefore, we have presented the actual situation of the flood disaster in our county in a disorganized manner, hoping that it will be published in your newspaper so that all sectors will know the magnitude of the disaster in our county and provide appropriate relief, so that hundreds of thousands of disaster victims in our county can survive. Awaiting death, we respectfully wish you peace. Disaster victims of Yancheng, Pan Deyu, Gao Shuchun, etc.

Qingjiang Jisheng Branch Appeals for Relief

The Qingjiang Qingsheng Branch's Second Letter to Mrs. Gailing Appealing for Relief reads: "Dear Mrs. Gailing, In our previous urgent telegram, we reported that Huaian and Siyang counties in northern Jiangsu were the first to suffer from the flood disaster, and the severity of the disaster was the greatest among other counties. Subsequently, Gaoyou and Shaobo also breached at the same time, and the tragic situation of the disaster victims was widely reported in the newspapers. We also learned that you have already issued a large sum of money to save them from starvation and drowning. Jiang Yun is grateful and admiring beyond words. The Shanghai Jisheng Relief Association and the Relief Association have entrusted our branch to handle emergency relief and seed distribution in the three counties of Huai, Huai, and Si. Each county will receive 20,000 yuan, totaling 60,000 yuan. We are currently preparing the procedures and will begin the investigation and distribution soon. However, the disaster is widespread, and the funds are limited, making it difficult to provide universal relief. We can only do our best. But the most important thing at present is that we are gradually entering late autumn, and winter is approaching. All the elderly and weak disaster victims in Huai, Yi, Si, You, and Shao who have nowhere to go must be provided with shelter. There are also homeless children who must be adopted. As for winter porridge factories to alleviate hunger, it is even more urgent and truly meritorious, with the aim of saving people. Now, we are writing to you again, hoping that you will continue to show great compassion and generously donate a large sum of money so that the survivors of the disaster in northern Jiangsu can be bathed in the sweet dew from the bottle. If you are willing to provide assistance, please send the relief funds directly to the Shanghai Flood Relief Association's three committee members, Wang Huangcheng, to be transferred to our branch for handling. Or, please send a special commissioner to Pu to preside over everything. Yuan Kai and Xilin will certainly follow and assist in the matter. Is there anything inappropriate? Please give us your precious guidance first, so that we can have a guideline. In this great disaster, saving people thoroughly is truly a way to leave a name for eternity and be immortal. Respectfully requesting your good health, Zhou Yuankai and Li Xilin of the Qingjiang Branch of the Chinese Jisheng Society."

The Director of the Hongkou Catholic Church Appeals for Relief

The Director of the Hongkou Catholic Church, Bian Detong, announced: "This year, floods are rampant, and over ten provinces are affected by the disaster, with tens of millions of people waiting for rescue. People from China and abroad are deeply saddened. As members of our church, we dare not lag behind others in this time of disaster relief and emergency assistance. In view of this, Bishop Hui convened a meeting of representatives from the four districts of Xujiahui, Yangjingbang, Dongjiadu, and Hongkou at the Hongkou Catholic Church on the 18th of this month to discuss relief methods. All the churches worked together with one heart and carried out the efforts together. Please ask all church members to donate generously to the disaster victims. We hereby send this letter, hoping that philanthropists, regardless of the amount, will do their best. I believe that our church members, who have always held the belief of loving others as ourselves, will certainly be eager to be at the forefront and enthusiastically rescue those in urgent need. Enclosed is a donation certificate. Please fill in the amount of your donation in the yuan and corner columns and send it along with the donation to our director. The disaster victims are in urgent need of help at this time. Please open your wallets as soon as possible and complete the donation within a week so that it can be collected and transferred to Bishop Hui for distribution, so that the disaster victims can benefit from it as soon as possible, expressing the intention of our church members to relieve their hunger and drowning. I respectfully appeal on their behalf, hoping for your consideration. September 22nd."

Below the Brothel

Two Prostitutes Flee Together 152

Beaten Due to Lack of Business

Wandering on the Road After Escaping

Hiding and Sobbing Together, They Were Rescued

Tian Jinbao, a woman from Hankou, is in her early twenties, and Shen Caibao, a woman from Changshu, is currently eighteen years old. Both women were abducted from their hometowns at the age of sixteen and sold by the abductors to a brothel at No. 4 Shengji Lane, Beichujiaqiao in the French Concession. For several years, they have been forced by the madam to go out every night with a maid escort to solicit customers. In addition to going to various amusement venues to attract customers at 5:00 PM every night, they often return to the brothel after 12:00 AM. The maid's surveillance is stricter than that of a prisoner. If they still do not have any customers to accompany them overnight, they must stand at the entrance of the alley, waiting until dawn. If no one inquires about them, the madam will whip them, even using rattan sticks to beat them severely, leaving the two women's bodies covered in bruises. They could not bear the abuse. On the 21st of this month, they were beaten severely again for failing to attract customers. The madam said, "The Mid-Autumn Festival is approaching, and you two unlucky stars are not making any business to cover expenses. Tomorrow, I will sell you to another place to see if you can still have a comfortable life." The two women were terrified upon hearing this and agreed to take advantage of the brothel's inattentiveness on the 22nd to escape secretly. However, because they were unfamiliar with the roads, they wandered the streets. That night, they fled aimlessly, waiting for dawn. Until about 10:00 PM the next day (the day before), the two women arrived near the Youche Wharf in Nanshi. They had not had any food or lodging for two days and were extremely tired from running day and night. At this point, they realized that although they had escaped from the fire pit, the future was uncertain, and they did not know where to settle down. Thinking of this, they could not help but feel sad and began to hide and sob together. The scene was witnessed by Liu Bingrong, a guard from the 18th post in the area. He brought the two women to the first branch of the first district. After the director of the branch preliminarily questioned them, the two women recounted their ordeal. The director ordered that a report be prepared and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for placement. Director Chen was extremely angry upon hearing this and immediately sent the matter to the rescue section of the second department for proper handling. He also dispatched personnel to thoroughly investigate the vicious madam of the brothel, arrest her, and deal with her severely. Furthermore, he investigated the source of the abductors and the families of the two women.

News of Direct Service on the Huzhou Steamer 154

The Beijing Road Taihu Steamer Company, in order to facilitate travel for passengers between Shanghai and Huzhou, has arranged for the Xinhu Steamer on the Xihu line to operate daily round trips, without stopping even at the end of the month. Last week, due to the overflow of river water between Daqian and Huzhou, smaller boats were temporarily used for transshipment. Now that the water level has receded, the connecting service will no longer be needed from the 23rd onwards. The large steamer can directly reach the Huzhou wharf, making travel between Shanghai and Huzhou more convenient.

Women's Work in Leprosy Relief 155

The Women's Support Association of the China Leprosy Relief Association held a regular meeting at the residence of Mrs. Xiao Zhiji yesterday. Over twenty people attended, including Mrs. Yan Fuqing, Mrs. Xi Boshou, Mrs. Cai Bingjiu, Ms. Chen Zhaoyue, and Ms. Xu. The meeting was chaired by Mrs. Zhang Jiabu, the president of the association. Mr. Wu Zhijian, the executive director, reported in detail on the progress of the Nanchang Leprosy Hospital and the plans to build a model leprosy clinic in Shanghai and a leprosy hospital in Xiamen. Subsequently, Pastor Shi Dingye, who came to Shanghai from Hainan, spoke about the preparations for the Qiongya Leprosy Hospital, stating that the preparations for the hospital have been underway for a year, but it was initially just an idea. Currently, the funds raised have reached 5,000 yuan, and the county government has allocated over 30 mu of wasteland as a base. In addition, there are building materials such as bricks and stones, worth about 2,000 yuan. Therefore, it is hoped that construction will be realized soon. He deeply hoped that the association would provide financial assistance to facilitate the start of construction as soon as possible.

Affairs of the Oriental Cultural Society 156

Drafting Documents on Japanese Invasion of Liaoning

Notifying Nationalities Worldwide

The Oriental Cultural Society recently convened a meeting of members at the residence of President Li Weihou to discuss strategies for development. At the meeting, the members elected executives and decided to solicit members in the country in October of this year, in accordance with the association's charter. Once the solicitation period is over, academic lectures will be organized, publications will be edited, and research will be conducted on the philosophy, art, religion, literature, and politics of various Oriental countries. Surveys will be conducted on the general situation of various Oriental countries, and the association's affairs will be recorded. In addition, at yesterday's special meeting, a detailed report was drafted on the Japanese invasion of Liaodong, translated into foreign languages, and sent to members in India, Turkey, Persia, Syria, Egypt, Annam, Siam, Afghanistan, and other countries to conduct practical publicity to avoid confusion caused by the Japanese.

YMCA Lecture Tonight 157

Dr. Schou Thet to Give Public Lecture

The great scientist Dr. Schou Thet, an American, suffered from severe hearing loss due to illness in his youth. Due to the pain he experienced, Dr. Schou Thet resolved to study the treatment of deafness to benefit those who suffer from the same condition around the world. Previously, Dr. Schou Thet invited local celebrities in the United States to organize an organization dedicated to serving the deaf. Now, Dr. Schou Thet is traveling in China, and the Shanghai YMCA has specially invited him to come to the meeting for a public lecture, hoping that enthusiastic people in Shanghai will continue Dr. Schou Thet's spirit and seek happiness for our compatriots. The lecture will be held at 7:30 PM on the evening of September 25th (Friday) in the YMCA auditorium. Those who wish to attend can go there at that time. Shanghai Chinese Christian YMCA.

Police Raid and Seize Bandits and Military Weapons 158

Shanghai Municipal Police detective Shang Wu learned that a large number of bandits were hiding in Room 324 of the Dahua Hotel on Xizang Road. He led Western detectives and all Chinese detectives to secretly raid the location around midnight and arrested nine people: Lin Ji, Cao Gusi, Hu Chuanfu, Ding Linqing, Liu Rongqing, Ai Jinrong, Wu Jinghui, Cai Menglin, and Chen Jikun. Liu Rongqing confessed that the military weapons were hidden in his home at No. 37 Rue Sainte Marie in the French Concession. Chinese and Western detectives and French police officers went there and seized two pistols and eight bullets. They then went to Room 7 of the Tiansheng Hotel at No. 63 Avenue Edward VII, and arrested Wu Tieming, Qian Guisheng, and two other people. They confessed that they had robbed a shop at No. 49 Beihai Road of 190 silver yuan at 11:00 AM on the 23rd of this month. The police chief ordered them to be detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang described the circumstances of the capture and stated that there were still accomplices at large, requesting a postponement. After Judge Feng questioned each of the defendants, he ordered them to be detained separately pending further investigation and questioning.

Verdict in Foreign Steamer Serge Theft Case 159

The Baonais Steamer, which was docked at the China Merchants Bureau North Wharf on Broadway Road, had 42 pieces of serge worth 15,000 yuan stolen between the 3rd and 4th of this month. The police were notified to investigate. Subsequently, Chinese and Western detectives from the Hongkou Police Department arrested over ten thieves and receivers of stolen goods, including Tang Xiaohangzi. Lawyer Zhang Tianyin represented the police and filed a lawsuit against them in the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The interrogation has concluded, and the details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong of the Third Criminal Court announced the verdict: Tang Xiaohangzi, Shang Wei, Yuan Da, Han Lide, Shang Liexi, Liu Jinbo, Zhu Xiaokouzi, Zhong Xiaosheng, Chen Erxi, and Chen Erbianzi were each sentenced to one year of imprisonment. Han Ke, Zhang Xiaozhang, and Dong Hong were each sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. Zhou Zhihe was sentenced to six months of imprisonment. Chen Xinsheng and Dai Junji were each sentenced to four months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the final verdict was determined, and two days of detention were allowed to offset one day of imprisonment.

Stone Bridge Collapses, Truck Carrying Goods Falls In 160

Three People Injured

The Baoshan Conservancy Office has been urgently repairing the Songkou Seawall for several days, so the sand, stones, timber, and other materials used are all transported from Shanghai by trucks. The day before yesterday afternoon, a truck fully loaded with timber was driven across the stone bridge over the city moat outside the North Gate of Baoshan. The bridge vibrated due to the excessive weight and suddenly collapsed. The truck fell into the river, injuring the driver and two laborers at the time. They were transported back to Shanghai for treatment by another truck. The fallen truck was finally lifted to the shore yesterday by a large number of laborers, but it was badly damaged.

Ms. Lin Chen Wrongfully Accused of Theft, Commits Suicide by Hanging 161

In the home of Li Yaoliang, a native of Changshu residing at No. 1, Sanheli, Nancang Street outside Xiaonanmen, was employed a female worker named Lin Chen, 47 years old, from Qingpu. Some days ago, she was suspected of theft based on someone's testimony. Unable to prove her innocence and overcome with anger, she secretly went to the drying platform in the evening and hanged herself with a trouser belt. The master of the house discovered this yesterday morning and immediately reported it to the Third Precinct of the First District. Police were dispatched to investigate and confirmed the facts. Qin Defang, the land head of the 23rd Pu, was summoned to report to the Local Court for examination. Prosecutor Yang and others arrived at the scene to examine the body and confirmed that it was indeed a suicide by hanging. The master of the house and the deceased's younger sister were taken to the court for questioning and then ordered to prepare the coffin for burial pending further investigation.

Call for Submissions for the 60th Anniversary Supplement of Shen Bao 164

To commemorate the 60th anniversary of this newspaper, a special anniversary supplement will be published. Its purpose is to enhance public interest in discussing issues and to reciprocate the readers' enthusiasm for supporting this newspaper. Starting in October, it will be published weekly, covering topics such as world affairs, politics, economics, and society. The topics for the first ten issues are listed below. Scholars and experts in the country are cordially invited to contribute insightful articles to enrich our publication and benefit society. We would be deeply grateful.

World China Shanghai Transportation Economy Water Conservancy Education Overseas Chinese Northeast Science

Submission Guidelines 165

1. Submissions must be within the scope of the topics predetermined by this publication.

2. Before submitting, contributors are requested to write to the 60th Anniversary Supplement Department of this newspaper to request a form, fill it out, and return it for special arrangement to avoid duplication.

3. The writing style should be popular and lively. The manuscript must be clearly written and punctuated.

4. If the submission is a translation, please attach the original text. If the original text is not convenient to attach, please provide detailed information about the title of the original work, the name of the author, and the date and place of publication.

5. Submissions that are published will be compensated appropriately, at a rate of three to ten yuan per thousand characters.

6. The amount of compensation for published submissions will be determined by this publication and will not be discussed in advance. If the contributor wishes to set their own amount, please state it when filling out the form.

7. Once a submission is published, the copyright belongs to this newspaper.

8. This publication reserves the right to make appropriate additions and deletions to submissions, but if the contributor does not wish others to make changes, they may state this when filling out the form.

9. To request a form, please write to the 60th Anniversary Supplement Department, Shen Bao, Shanghai.

Reader Correspondence

Questioning the Monk Dian Chan (Seeking Refuge in Buddhism to Study Buddhist Doctrine) 166

I am a frustrated young man looking for a way to solve my problems. Some people advise me not to be discouraged and to strive in my career, while others invite me to seek the path of emptiness. Ultimately, driven by my circumstances, I have decided to seek refuge in Buddhism, but I need to prepare in advance. I have heard of a "Commentary on the Mahavairocana Sutra," but I don't know where to buy it. Also, I am not very clear on how to start studying Buddhist doctrine. My wavering spirit does not know which path to take. Your newspaper is all-encompassing and points out the way for those who are lost. Please use your valuable space to guide me and also provide guidance to others who are equally frustrated or on the wrong path. This will not only benefit me but also the masses.

(Reply) Your decision to seek refuge in Buddhism because you are frustrated and discouraged is fundamentally wrong. As the ancients said, "Becoming a monk is a matter for great men, not something that princes and generals can do." Sakyamuni, as a crown prince, became a monk entirely to solve the great problem of life and death. Therefore, he gave up his throne and personally practiced and attained enlightenment, becoming a Buddha. Then he went everywhere to preach and save all beings. This spirit of self-sacrifice to save the world is not something that princes and generals can do. From the Tang Dynasty to the Ming Dynasty, there was a system in our country where anyone who wanted to become a monk had to pass an examination by the government. They had to be qualified in terms of learning and aspirations before being granted a certificate allowing them to become a monk, called a "Dudie." In the early Qing Dynasty, this system was abolished, and people were allowed to become monks at will, turning the pure Buddhist community almost into a haven for fugitives and creating countless idle monks. This is entirely a social ill. If politics is on the right track and the social components are healthy, this kind of illness needs to be treated quickly. Since you are an ambitious young man, would you be willing to become a parasite of society? Look at Japan, which is also a Buddhist country. They can use the great fearless spirit of Buddhism to cultivate healthy citizens. Their monks are learned and can guide the people, which is very different from the situation in our country. Therefore, to study Buddhist doctrine, you need to know the true spirit of Buddhism. As for the "Commentary on the Mahavairocana Sutra," the newly revived Esoteric Buddhism Association in Huzhou is selling it, but it is a profound esoteric text that is definitely not for beginners to understand. If you want to know how to get started with Buddhist doctrine, you should first read a few books, listed below. After reading them, you will naturally find a way in.

"An Introduction to Buddhism," published by Zhonghua Book Company, price 8 jiao, written by Jiang Zuoqiao

"How to Study Buddhism," published by Commercial Press, price 8 jiao, written by Lu Ji

"A Brief History of Indian Buddhism," published by Commercial Press, price 1 yuan 2 jiao, written by Lu Cheng

Reader Correspondence Guidelines for Shen Bao 167

The staff of this newspaper firmly believes that all readers have certain personal problems that urgently need to be discussed. Based on the spirit of serving society, the staff is willing to act as consultants and offer sincere suggestions in writing. If readers can obtain appropriate solutions, reduce difficulties, and increase happiness as a result, we would be greatly pleased.

1. The problems that readers wish to discuss with the staff of this newspaper are temporarily limited to three categories: seeking knowledge...

2. When writing, please first state your full name, gender, age, occupation, (or place of study, grade,) native place, and mailing address (please provide details even when continuing correspondence, in case the previous letter does not reach us). Then, start a new paragraph and state the problem you wish to discuss. The writing should be detailed, accurate, and easy to understand. Please write "Reader Correspondence Department, Shen Bao" on the outside of the envelope and attach the corresponding amount of return postage. When writing, please cut out the special stamp of the "Reader Correspondence" column of this newspaper and paste it on the upper left corner of the letter as proof of purchase.

3. The method of handling letters received by this newspaper:

A. We will respect the wishes of readers. We will comply with any requests to not publish the response in the newspaper or to not disclose names in the response.

B. If the letter does not state how the response should be handled, but the staff believes that the response to one person has value for everyone, it will be published in the newspaper.

C. If the letter states that the response should be published in the newspaper, but it is limited by space, we can only publish the key points, or may not be able to publish it at all, or may have to delay publication because the problem requires further consideration. We ask for your understanding. However, if we cannot answer in the newspaper, we will still answer by mail.

Chen Qiufeng Wants to Separate from Her Mother-in-Law 168

Otherwise, She Refuses to Live with Her Husband

Zhang Xuanzhong, a native of Yin County, Ningbo, resides at No. 8, Yifang, Bao'an Road, Dixiwei Road. He works as a clerk at the Da Lai Yang Firm. He married Chen Qiufeng. Initially, they were harmonious, but after a short time, Chen Qiufeng ran away with her belongings. Zhang then entrusted lawyer Chen Bingxing to post a warning in the newspaper. After repeated investigations, it was discovered that Chen Qiufeng was hiding in a certain place. Zhang went to pick her up, but was unsuccessful. He then hired lawyer Chen to file a petition with the First Special District Court requesting cohabitation. Both parties were summoned and appeared in court. Chen Qiufeng did not object to cohabitation, but demanded that she must live separately from her mother-in-law. Therefore, the mediation failed. Zhang then formally filed a lawsuit. The Special Court transferred the case to the Shanghai Local Court for trial. The defendant also hired lawyer Liu Zuwang to file a defense and a counterclaim. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shenglu held a special session in the Third Court to hear the case. The plaintiff, Zhang Xuanzhong, appeared in court with his lawyer, Chen Bingxing. The defendant, Chen Qiufeng, did not appear, but was represented by lawyer Liu Zuwang. According to Zhang Xuanzhong's testimony, he is 25 years old and a native of Ningbo. The defendant, Chen Qiufeng, is indeed his wife. They were married in their hometown in 1926 and then came to Shanghai together. After living together for only a few months, she returned to Ningbo on some pretext. This time, she left without saying goodbye. Now that the lawsuit has been filed, she insists on living separately from my mother, but in fact, it is difficult to agree to this because my income is meager and I rely on it to support my elderly mother and younger siblings. If we live separately, my mother and younger siblings will not be taken care of. (Asked) Who was the matchmaker? (Answered) Zhang Guixiao, a public uncle in my clan. The judge ordered that he be invited to the next hearing. Next, the defendant's lawyer stated Chen Qiufeng's age and origin, saying that the defendant is 23 years old this year, a native of Ningbo, and lives at Chunhe Coal Shop in Dongtingshan Lane, Guanqiao, Nanshi, Shanghai. The plaintiff requested a divorce in the Special Court, but then changed it to cohabitation. However, the defendant does not want a divorce because she has a bad relationship with her mother-in-law, so she requests to live separately. Previously, when the defendant returned to Ningbo, the plaintiff posted a warning in the newspaper, accusing the defendant of running away with her belongings. However, the plaintiff had sent two letters, one to the defendant's brother and one to the plaintiff's uncle, which proves that the plaintiff knew the defendant's whereabouts. How can he say that she ran away? Moreover, the defendant had been ill and spent a lot of money. Now she is counterclaiming for living expenses and medical expenses before the lawsuit, totaling 450 yuan, and 35 yuan per month for future living expenses. The judge ordered that the hearing be continued.

Assassination Case of French Merchant to be Judged 169

Zhong Ziqing Released

On the afternoon of the 15th of last month, at the New French Concession West Xinqiao Street No. 113 Fa Shang New Hotel, a reporter claiming to be Wang Xi opened room number two. Around 6 p.m., a robbery and murder case occurred. Xia Yongsheng and a Mr. Xue were killed on the spot, and Jiang Yihan (Chen Yiming) and Zhong Ziqing were injured. After the murderer escaped, the injured were taken to Renji Hospital by the police. Chen Yiming died the next day due to his injuries. Zhong Ziqing's injuries were not fatal, and he was fortunate to survive. The bodies of the three deceased were examined and collected by the police after reporting to the court. After the incident, the next day, the French police special agency captured the murderer Yan Jinbiao from Jiangbei and suspects Dai Yunhong and Yan's mistress, Ms. Zhang, and sent them to the Second Special Court. According to Yan's confession, he was hired by Li Guocheng to commit the shooting murder and also admitted to committing three robbery cases in the French Concession. He was ordered to be detained for further questioning after Zhong Ziqing's injuries healed. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Now that Zhong's wound has healed, the police sent him to the court yesterday. Judge Luo Renji sat in the criminal court for further questioning. First, police lawyer Gu Shouxi explained the case, stating that the police found no criminal evidence against Zhong Ziqing, so no prosecution was filed and requesting a hearing. Zhong Ziqing testified that he is 41 years old, a native of Yangzhou, and used to run a shoe store. This year, he served as a conscription committee member of the Ninth Division and resigned on August 6. On the afternoon of the 15th, he was invited by the deceased Xia Yongsheng to the Fa Shang Hotel to discuss a job as an inspector on a small steamer. When he arrived at the hotel, he had a headache due to the cold and was lying in bed. Less than ten minutes later, someone came and started shooting. He was shot four times, and his left arm bone was broken. Although he has recovered, the wound under his left shoulder has not healed and is still festering. He does not know the defendant Yan Jinbiao, but only knows Xia Yongsheng. He has always been upright and requests an investigation. Yan Jinbiao testified that he does not know Zhong. The judge then ordered the debate to begin. First, police lawyer Gu Shouxi argued that the defendant Yan Jinbiao had confessed to one murder and three robbery crimes, and the evidence was conclusive. He requested that the case be handled in accordance with Articles 246 and 383 of the Criminal Law. The defendants were represented by lawyer Wang Shizong, who was appointed by the court to provide legal aid. He argued that it could not be proven whether the murder was committed by Yan or by the fugitive murderer. However, the murder was due to an uneven distribution of loot. Since Yan's responsibility for the murder cannot be proven, he should be given leniency. The second and third defendants were completely unrelated. Dai only went to inquire about the news after the event, and Ms. Zhang was only Yan's mistress. They should be declared innocent. The judge also questioned Tang A’gen, a waiter at the Chunjiang Hotel at 309 Caishi Street, who testified that on August 14, someone opened room 21, but he did not remember the face. Yan testified that he did not open the room at the Chunjiang Hotel. Judge Luo announced the end of the debate and that the verdict would be announced on the morning of October 1. Zhong Ziqing was released and ordered to appear in court at any time if summoned, and to report any change of address. Zhong thanked the judge and left.

Daughter of Gatekeeper Arrested, Kidnapped 170

Taken to Changzhou to Cohabit

Person Involved Detained for Investigation

Wang Jingyu, a native of Shandong, lives at No. 114, Alcock Road. He works as a gatekeeper No. 1235 for the police. His daughter, Xiuying, is 20 years old and was engaged to Lu Caifu last year. However, Lu does not engage in proper work. Last year, he was sentenced to one year in prison by the court for robbery, so the marriage has been delayed. Yesterday morning at 6:30, Lu and several others hired car No. 18075 from the Jinxing Motor Company on Yangshupu Road and drove to Wang's house. When Xiuying went out, they dragged her into the car and sped away. At that time, a girl named Ruan Xiangyun happened to be going out to get water and, seeing this, ran to tell Wang Jingyu, who reported it to the Huishan Police Station. After investigation by detective Zhao Duansheng, it was learned that Dong Xiting, a native of Changzhou, was involved in the case. Dong was arrested and, after questioning, confessed that he was invited by Lu to help. Now Wang Xiuying has been taken to Changzhou by Lu and others to cohabit. The police also summoned Ruan Xiangyun and the driver, Zhu Zhaomeng. Ruan identified Dong as being at the scene at the time, and Zhu confirmed that the car was hired by Dong and the fare was paid by Dong.
