Since it is still necessary to arrest the accomplices, he requested permission to reschedule the hearing. Ruan Xiangyun and others then proved everything. The defendant testified that he was an aircraft mechanic in the Xiamen Aviation Team and was deceived by Lu Caifu. Judge Shen Bingrong reviewed the confession and ordered that the case be rescheduled for further hearing.

Ministry of Industry

Revised Detailed Rules for Raw Silk Inspection 171

Quality Inspection Temporarily Free of Charge

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has been implementing raw silk inspection for more than a year. The Ministry of Industry has now revised the detailed rules for raw silk inspection of the bureau, changing them to thirteen articles of the Regulations for Raw Silk Inspection, which have been promulgated by the Ministry and implemented. The original detailed rules have been abolished. Furthermore, silk factories in various places do not pay much attention to the quality inspection of raw silk, so it is impossible to distinguish the quality of the products, which is a major obstacle to improving the silk industry. In order to promote the improvement of raw silk quality, the ministry has stipulated in the aforementioned regulations that quality inspection will be temporarily free of charge to encourage it. The regulations are as follows: Regulations for Raw Silk Inspection by the Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, promulgated by decree of the Ministry of Industry on August 20, 1931. (Article 1) These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Articles 2, Item 3, and 21 of the Provisional Regulations for Commodity Inspection (hereinafter referred to as the Regulations). (Article 2) Raw silk inspection is divided into the following two categories: (1) Quantity inspection, including gross weight, net weight, and degumming; (2) Quality inspection, including uniformity, cleanliness, clarity, cohesion, tenacity, and elongation (single and double strand). (Article 3) All raw silk exported abroad shall comply with the provisions of these regulations, be inspected by the Inspection Bureau to obtain the gross weight, and be issued a certificate before being allowed to declare for export. (Net weight and degumming in quantity inspection and quality inspection shall be requested freely by merchants.) (Article 4) Raw silk trade shall comply with the gross weight inspected by the Inspection Bureau as the standard for calculating value. (Article 5) The following raw silk items are exempt from inspection: (1) Diplopia and waste silk; (2) Non-domestic products; (3) Sample silk within one dan; (4) Non-sale items for competitions or scientific research. The aforementioned diplopia and waste silk shall be marked on the outside of the package. (Article 6) When a merchant or trader requests inspection, they shall fill out an inspection request form, submit it to the Inspection Bureau along with the inspection fee for the raw silk, and obtain a receipt for the inspection separately. (Article 7) The sampling method for raw silk inspection is as follows: (1) Gross weight inspection: (1) The number of packages to be inspected shall be 40% of the total number of packages in each batch. If there is a remainder, it shall be proportionally increased. (2) Two samples of silk shall be taken from each piece, each sample weighing 450 cm. (3) No more than two strips shall be drawn from each roasted strip package. (4) The samples shall be placed in lead trays, one tied with a red label and one tied with a white label. (2) Degumming inspection: (1) The sample strip shall be one-tenth of the weight of each batch. If there is a remainder, it shall be proportionally increased. (2) Ten hanks shall be selected from each piece of raw silk, and 100 cm shall be taken from the ten hanks as samples, divided into two parts, one of which shall be tied with a cotton tape label. (3) Quality inspection: (1) For those that must be inspected on each piece, at least ten silk strips shall be sampled. When drawing, the inside of the piece shall be covered, but no more than one strip per package. (2) For each batch of raw silk, those that need to be inspected in detail in five or ten pieces shall be sampled four strips from each piece, but no more than one strip per package. (9) For each batch of raw silk, if there are more than ten pieces, ten pieces shall be regarded as one batch, and each batch shall be marked with consecutive numbers, and samples shall be taken separately in accordance with the previous method. If there are less than five pieces, samples shall be drawn equally according to the number of pieces. (The samples taken in items (1) and (2) of this section may be used for several types of inspections. (Article 8) The order of inspection shall be based on the order of reporting for inspection and shall be completed within 14 hours after receiving the inspection request form and raw silk. (Article 9) The unpacking and packing of raw silk during inspection shall be done by the Inspection Bureau, but the person reporting for inspection shall be informed to be present. (Article 10) After the raw silk inspection is completed, the gross weight inspection shall be carried out in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the regulations, and a mark shall be added to each package of raw silk, and an export certificate shall be issued. (Article 11) The raw silk sent to the bureau for inspection shall be returned to the bureau with the original receipt after the inspection is completed. If there is a delay, the Inspection Bureau may return the raw silk to the person reporting for inspection, and the shipping fee shall be borne by the person reporting for inspection. (Article 12) The amount of inspection fee is as follows: (1) Quantity inspection: (A) Gross weight factory silk, 2 yuan per piece, tribute silk 1 yuan per piece; (B) Net weight 1 yuan per piece; (C) Degumming each time (sampling silk ten skeins using one hundred centimeters) 2 yuan (2) Quality inspection is temporarily free of charge; (3) Warehouse rent is 5 jiao per piece per month. If it is less than one month, it shall be calculated as one month. (Article 13) These regulations shall come into force from the date of promulgation.

Harbor Quarantine Office

Publication of Cholera Prevention Report 172

No. 9

The National Harbor Quarantine Office published its ninth cholera prevention report, stating that: (1) The cholera situation in Shanghai this past week (September 12 to 19) has not improved or worsened much. There were 40 cases in the Chinese area, with no deaths. However, there were 30 cases in the International Settlement (2 foreigners), with one death. There were 6 cases in the French Concession, with no deaths. In total, there were 76 cases this past week, with only one death, proving that the effectiveness of scientific vaccination is not insignificant. (2) There have been reports of fatal cholera cases in the disaster areas of Wuchang and Hankou. (The Heishan refugee camp has already built accommodations for hundreds of people, and there are approximately 30 cases in Hankou City.) Typhoid fever and dysentery have long been prevalent diseases in the area. Since the discovery of cholera, the epidemic prevention police have been performing their duties in difficult situations. Sitting in grass sheds, the disaster victims are enduring hunger and waiting to die, and their resistance to the epidemic is very weak. Therefore, the authorities must do their best to prevent it. According to medical reports, the distribution of vaccinations for cholera and typhoid fever has been expanded to all disaster victims in the refugee camps. Due to the lack of water and the large number of flies, epidemic prevention and disaster relief work is extremely difficult. (3) The medical officer stationed in Songhu found several cholera patients on a Hankou steamer some days ago. For example, on September 18, there were 6 suspected cholera cases. The patients have been transferred to the Wusong Anti-Epidemic Hospital of this office. Three of them have been proven by bacterial examination to be true cholera, but all have been cured after treatment. These patients all seem to come from Xiantao Town in Mianyang County, about 360 miles west of Hankou. (4) Hankou has been declared a cholera epidemic area by this office. All ships from that area must anchor at designated locations for inspection when passing through Nanjing and Wusong. All passengers who have not been vaccinated should be vaccinated before disembarking. (5) On September 18, Japanese militarists invaded areas of our country in southern Manchuria, such as Liaoyang, Andong, Niuzhuang, Changchun, and Jilin. It is inhumane to take advantage of our country's disaster. Therefore, the Flood Relief Committee has refused to cooperate with Japanese medical officers and has returned all disaster relief items donated by Japan, such as money, food, medicine, and hospital ships, to show its displeasure with the militarists' atrocities and dispel the enthusiasm of Japanese philanthropists.

Tongzhou Buoy Moved 176

Notice No. 1012 of the Marine Affairs Section of the Customs states: This patrol service has investigated the movement of the Tongzhou buoy within the jurisdiction of the Zhenjiang Customs, as well as the installation of warning lights, and has listed the situation as follows: The Tongzhou buoy has now been moved. From the new location, the Tongzhou Customs is at 58 degrees north and west (according to the compass direction), at a distance of 4.45 English nautical miles. In order to assist ships passing between the Liuhai Sandbank North Bank light buoy and the Tongzhou buoy at night, and to avoid the Qingtian Reef, two unlisted warning lights are hung directly on the Tongzhou buoy, about twelve feet apart, and will be opened on September 30 this year for implementation, without further notice. The line between the Liuhai Sandbank North Bank light buoy and the Tongzhou light buoy marks the middle of the navigation channel, about four-tenths of an English nautical mile from the north bank of the Qingtian Reef. Please refer to Chinese Navy Hydrographic Chart No. 143 for clarity. All ships should pay attention and remember this to avoid negligence. This notice is hereby issued. Patrol Service Hee Lyman, September 22.

Soldiers Using Counterfeit Money 177

Sentenced to Five Years of Imprisonment

Soldier Meng Zhaoru (alias Wang Yucai) from Anhui, carrying forty-six counterfeit five-yuan banknotes with the intention of using them in the city, was apprehended by Chinese Constable No. 2264 of the International Settlement Police Station on North Henan Road at 6:15 PM on May 4th of this year. He was handed over to the First Special District Court. During the interrogation, the judge stated that Meng was an active military member and thus the court would not handle the case. After a final decision, he and the counterfeit money would be transferred to the Garrison Headquarters for investigation. The police station, disagreeing with this ruling, appealed. The Second Higher Branch Court, after deliberation, overturned the original ruling and sent the case back to the original court for review. Consequently, the police station sent Meng back to the Special Court for questioning. A verdict was reserved. Yesterday morning, the verdict was announced by Judge Feng Shide in the Second Criminal Court. The main text of the verdict stated that Meng Zhaoru, intending to use and possessing counterfeit general banknotes, was sentenced to five years of imprisonment. The number of days spent in detention before the final judgment will be deducted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The forty-six counterfeit banknotes are to be confiscated.

Shen Bao Local Supplement 181

Social News

Aviation in Malaya by Qiu Bincun 182

Aviation is a new industry that has emerged only in the last few decades. Since the rise of aviation, the concept of national sovereignty has also changed. Previously, the general understanding of national sovereignty was limited to territorial and maritime sovereignty. Now, we believe that national sovereignty should include airspace in addition to territory and sea. In ancient times, during the closed-door era, national military strength relied entirely on the army. In recent times, after the opening of maritime borders, national military strength focused on the navy. In the future, with the development of aviation, national military strength will not rely on the army or the navy, but on the air force. Moreover, aviation occupies not only the most important position in military affairs, but also the most important position in politics, diplomacy, economics, transportation, and culture. Therefore, countries around the world are competing to develop the aviation industry in preparation for political, military, economic, and cultural struggles. In Southeast Asia, with the independent government of Siam and the resident governments of Britain, the Netherlands, France, and the United States, aviation is of course being pursued vigorously and without reservation. The author now discloses the situation of the aviation industry in British Malaya to show a glimpse of its progress. While it is said to be about the aviation industry in Malaya, it is actually related to Britain, India, Australia, Siam, the Dutch East Indies, and other places.

(I) Air Routes Between Malaya and Britain and Australia

Britain's colonies are all over the five continents. Fortunately, there are twelve important colonies in the world. To protect these colonies, Britain has adopted the so-called Three C Policy. The Three C Policy is Cape Town, Cairo, Calcutta. More specifically, it means that Britain, starting from Europe, must occupy Cape Town in Africa, then Cairo in Egypt, and then Calcutta in Asia in order to protect the colonies along the way, especially the two pieces of fat, India and Australia. Therefore, its air routes also follow the good Three C Policy and set up various networks. The matters of aviation and flights between Malaya and Britain and Australia are described as follows:

The first flight of the British-Australian air mail service has already begun. The aircraft City of Cairo, responsible for the flight from Karachi to Darwin, arrived in Singapore the day before yesterday afternoon and left yesterday morning. Governor Sir Cecil Clementi specially entrusted the aircraft to bring a letter, wishing success to British-Australian aviation. The British Colonial Secretary, Lord Passfield, also sent a letter with the Deputy Governor, Mr. Scott, which was delivered the day before yesterday. The letter is translated as follows:

Dear Mr. Scott,

The British-Australian air mail service has now opened. The connection between Britain and Malaya will be closer, and transportation between the two places will be faster, which is a hopeful reality. I am very pleased to be able to express my satisfaction on the occasion of the first flight of the British-Australian airmail service through Singapore. I believe that the residents of the Straits Settlements and the Federated Malay States will also be very satisfied with this move. The Malayan government can vigorously support the British-Australian scheduled flights to achieve their goal of success. I am confident that they will do their best to support it in this difficult economic environment.

Lord Passfield, British Colonial Secretary, April 1, 1931. After receiving this letter, Deputy Governor Scott immediately replied to Passfield by telegram. The telegram said, "The letter delivered by the British-Australian airmail on April 1 has been received and is greatly appreciated. The Malayan government has taken note of and is prepared to vigorously support the Imperial airmail service to Australia to achieve its goal of success, in response to your sincere wishes."

It is noted that the aircraft City of Cairo, which arrived in Singapore the day before yesterday and left yesterday, is responsible for the journey from Karachi to Darwin. It left Seletar Airfield early yesterday morning, hoping to arrive in Surabaya by late afternoon or evening yesterday. If this is not possible, it will stop in Batavia.

There were four bags of letters loaded in Singapore destined for Australia, and one bag destined for Surabaya. There were hundreds of letters destined for Australia, including 489 sent from Singapore, 169 sent from the Federated Malay States, 114 sent from Kedah, and 84 sent from Johor.

The aircraft is scheduled to arrive in Darwin tomorrow (Sunday), which is the fifteenth day after leaving Britain. The journey of 11,194 miles only took 15 days, which is very fast. It will then leave Darwin on April 27 and return to Britain, arriving at Croydon Aerodrome around May 14. Therefore, the aircraft will come to Singapore again around May 29.

We have already described the trial use of British-Australian airmail in the previous paragraphs. Now we translate the various regulations and notices issued by the Secretariat of the Post Office of the Straits Settlements and the Federated Malay States regarding the flight of this aircraft as follows:

A. All mail related to this second British-Australian airmail trial flight will be collected in Singapore on April 17 (first time) and May 8 (second time) of this year and forwarded to Surabaya, Java, and various parts of Australia. B. The postage for all mail will be the standard postage plus airmail postage as follows:

(1) For mail sent via Surabaya to Java or other parts of the Dutch East Indies: 12 cents per half ounce.

(2) For mail sent to Darwin: 16 cents per half ounce.

(3) For mail sent to other parts of Australia and New Zealand: 40 cents per half ounce.

C. Mail returning from Australia to Britain will be collected in Singapore on April 30 (first time) and May 20 (second time) and forwarded to Delhi and London. The postage for all mail will be the standard postage plus airmail postage as follows:

(1) For mail sent via Delhi to various parts of India: 16 cents per half ounce.

(2) For mail sent via London to various parts of Britain and Europe and North America: 42 cents per half ounce.

D. Letters, postcards, printed matter, merchandise, and parcels can all be sent by this aircraft, but only by registered mail and not by insurance.

E. In addition to following the usual mailing procedures, mail sent by this aircraft must also be affixed with a blue airmail label (available at all post offices) in the upper left corner and must include the following words:

(1) For mail sent to Java, Australia, and New Zealand: "By Air Mail British Australian Flight"

(2) For mail sent via Delhi to various parts of India: "By Air Mail Singapore Delhi"

(3) For mail sent via London to various parts of Britain and Europe and North America: "By Air Mail Singapore London"

F. The above airmail postage is in addition to the standard postage. If the mail is registered, the registration fee should also be paid according to the usual regulations, and then the above airmail postage should be added. If the regulations are not followed, the mail will be shelved and not delivered.

G. All mail from outside Singapore must arrive in Singapore by night train the night before mailing to facilitate inspection and mailing to avoid mistakes.

(II) Aviation Between Malaya and the Netherlands

We have briefly described the matters of flights between Malaya and Britain and Australia. Here, we will specifically discuss aviation between Malaya and the Netherlands. When aviation in Southeast Asia reaches its peak, Java in the Dutch East Indies will be at its center. The scheduled mail flights (twice a week) from the Dutch capital to Batavia have already dropped off mail for Malaya at the Alor Setar Airport. It has been decided that the route will be extended to Australia by the end of this month. This plan to extend the route has been strongly supported by many large businesses in the Dutch East Indies, who have decided to raise 40,000 Dutch guilders to support the development of this project. This plan was originally initiated by Dutch Air Force Officer Batiste. In the future, the aircraft transferring mail to Australia will be piloted by Batiste. The aircraft is a Fokker F7A six-seater aircraft named BbelTasman (the same model as the Cross aircraft piloted by Kingsford Smith and the mail aircraft between Singapore and Batavia). In addition to Batiste as the pilot, there is also a second-class engineer, Moro, as an assistant. Moro is an employee of the Dutch East Indies Aviation Department and also serves as the aircraft's radio equipment engineer and repairman. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement 183

Book Review

On Urban Zoning 184

— Gao Wei

By Dong Xiujia

"On Urban Zoning" by Mr. Dong Xiujia is a specialized book discussing the issue of urban zoning systems. The author is one of the leading municipal scholars in the country. Here, the author not only strongly advocates the necessity of urban zoning but also earnestly indicates the principles of urban zoning. Originally, municipal science was a science that emerged in the 20th century, so the urban zoning system is a method recently invented by cities around the world. Its evolutionary history is very short, but the fact that this urban zoning system has been adopted by various countries proves that this system is of great benefit to municipal administration and cannot be ignored by us municipal scholars.

We know that when cities in various countries were first constructed, they adopted a laissez-faire approach in order to attract a large population. There were no laws or regulations to restrain them, so there were no restrictions on buildings in the city. As a result, all buildings were uneven in height, unequal in size, and land use was chaotic. As a result, the sunlight and air for citizens, shops, and residences were suffocated, and public health was out of the question. However, "In recent years, the population of cities in various countries has increased daily, and industry and commerce have developed. City residents are clustered in the city without order, resulting in housing problems and health problems. Cities in various countries, feeling the non-existence of the laissez-faire approach, have followed each other in advocating the urban zoning system. The first to adopt it were cities in Germany, followed by other cities in Europe. Now, countries in the Americas and Japan have also stipulated zoning laws and earnestly implemented them. After implementation, citizens live in separate zones in an orderly manner, urban health is gradually improved, and citizens' lives are also improving day by day." (Preface) It can be seen that the practical function of the urban zoning system and its influence are indeed extremely great.

The book is divided into four chapters: 1. Introduction; 2. Zoning Law According to Land Use; 3. Zoning Law According to Building Capacity; 4. Conclusion. The author first describes the process of various countries adopting the zoning system and the main points of their zoning system, then discusses the zoning system of our major cities, and finally compares the various systems to explain the advantages and disadvantages, so as to provide a reference for our cities.

In the introduction, the author explains that the current division of urban zoning in various countries is generally stipulated by law. As for the power to stipulate zoning, in general, unitary countries are authorized by the central government to cities, while federal governments are authorized by the governments of each state to cities. We must recognize this legal basis. Secondly, the author introduces the theories of urban zoning by municipal scholars from various countries, such as Williams, Bassett, and Nolen. The author also criticizes the fact that citizens of our cities cannot understand the meaning of zoning.

"Zoning Law According to Land Use," the author first introduces the adoption of zoning laws according to land use by various countries and the main points of their zoning laws. According to this system, the most widely adopted city is Frankfurt am Main in Germany. Later, cities in Germany adopted it, and it spread to Switzerland, Norway, and Sweden. Britain also adopted it in 1909. Now, Canada, the United States, and Japan have also mostly adopted this zoning principle. Then, the author describes the adoption of zoning laws according to land use by our cities and the main points of their zoning. The following are the author's opinions provided in "The Principles of Urban Zoning System According to Land Use":

The author advocates that when this zoning law is adopted, it can be divided into "heavy industrial zone, light industrial zone, large and small commercial zone, residential zone, and municipal administrative zone, etc." At the same time, for clarity, the author details several principles for dividing various zones: (1) Areas near railways and rivers should be designated as large commercial or industrial zones because of their convenient transportation; (2) Areas close to mountains and rivers or with more forests should be designated as residential zones; (3) A small commercial zone should be delineated near residential zones; (4) Parks, lakes, ponds, and small hills and mounds in various parts of the city should be specially preserved and repaired and cultivated for citizens to visit and rest, so that the city air can be harmonized; (5) The central point of the city should be designated as the city center zone, and the municipal administrative zone can be close to the large commercial zone, or it can be stipulated to be attached to the large commercial zone; (6) The residential zones of a city can be distributed in various places, but in any case, they cannot be close to the large commercial zone or industrial zone; (7) Scenic spots should be drawn near the city to give the city the flavor of a garden city; (8) Within the possible scope, the old commercial zone should be temporarily preserved, and after the new urban area is developed, the appropriate zone should be stipulated according to the trend of development.

"Zoning Law According to Building Capacity" was also initiated in German cities. Its purpose is to improve urban health, eliminate fire hazards, and increase the magnificence and beauty of street appearance. In recent years, most countries in Europe and the United States have also approved of it. In "Zoning Law According to Building Area," the author also first describes the general state of adoption by cities in various countries, and then describes the adoption situation of our cities. In "Zoning Law According to Building Height," the author also describes it as usual. As for the principles of this zoning law, the author believes that there should also be the following standards:

For those belonging to zoning according to building area: (1) The standard should be the location of the land, and the area occupied by the buildings in the city should not be stipulated as the same; (2) The standard should be the size of the base, and the area occupied by the size should not be limited to the same; (3) The land in the central area of a city should be occupied by less area by the buildings, and the land outside should be more; (4) The land in the middle of a base should be occupied by less area by the buildings, and the land in the outer circle should be more; (5) The land occupied by the buildings in the industrial and commercial zones can be more, and the land in the residential zones can be less; For those belonging to zoning according to building height: (1) The height of buildings in residential zones should be the lowest; (2) The commercial zone can be higher than the residential and industrial zones; (3) The industrial zone can be slightly higher than the residential zone; (4) The height of buildings on two sides of the street should be slightly lower than the height of buildings on one side of the street; (5) The height of wooden buildings should be lower than the height of brick buildings; (6) The height of brick buildings should be lower than the height of reinforced concrete buildings; (7) The height of buildings in the outer circle area can be slightly higher than that in the middle area; (8) The height of buildings at the corner of a base can be slightly higher than that in the middle.

The above points should be paid attention to by those who manage urban construction.

Now, the number of cities in our country that have established municipal administration is increasing day by day. "It is naturally very good for our cities to adopt the zoning system now, but two points should be noted: First, before dividing the height of buildings and stipulating the area of building zones, the area should be divided according to land use, and the area divided according to land use should be the standard for the height and area of buildings in each zone, so that the restrictions in each zone can be appropriate and the needs of each zone can be suitable. Second, attention should be paid to the future, not the past. Although the area has been divided and the height and area of buildings have been stipulated, old buildings that interfere with the zoning system can only be allowed to exist temporarily. When they are rebuilt in the future, they should be ordered to be rebuilt in accordance with the regulations. They cannot be ordered to be rebuilt in accordance with the zoning regulations after the zoning system has been established, which violates the purpose of the law not pursuing the past and only causes various disputes. However, new buildings should always be built in accordance with the zoning regulations, and should not be leniently accommodated. This is what is meant by paying attention to the future and not pursuing the past."
